  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_29d83f8b-ef69-45cd-8f8b-0e87afe74b40'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

Now, in the glittering capitals and carefree playgrounds of post-war Europe, Demiris sets his deadly sights on Catherine -- and the single, treacherous secret whose shattering truth is known to her alone...</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer433772517" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18101392005879457372">Memories of Midnight (Midnight #2), Sidney Sheldon<br/>Memories of Midnight, sometimes known as The Other Side of Midnight (Book 2), is a 1990 novel by Sidney Sheldon. The plot of Memories of Midnight takes off from the ending of The Other Side of Midnight, where Catherine Douglas is recovering in a convent. The world except Constantin Demiris, known as Costa, thinks that Catherine has been killed by her husband, Larry Douglas, and his mistress, Noelle Page. But Catherine wants to discover herself an</span>
  <span id="freeText18101392005879457372" style="display:none">Memories of Midnight (Midnight #2), Sidney Sheldon<br />Memories of Midnight, sometimes known as The Other Side of Midnight (Book 2), is a 1990 novel by Sidney Sheldon. The plot of Memories of Midnight takes off from the ending of The Other Side of Midnight, where Catherine Douglas is recovering in a convent. The world except Constantin Demiris, known as Costa, thinks that Catherine has been killed by her husband, Larry Douglas, and his mistress, Noelle Page. But Catherine wants to discover herself and know who she is. The only thing she knows is that her name is Catherine Alexander. She requests to see the world outside the convent to reveal her past. This request is granted by the Sister of the convent, but only after getting the approval from their multimillionaire mentor, Constantin Demiris. ...<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز هفتم ماه ژانویه سال 1997 میلادی<br />عنوان: خاطرات نیمه شب؛ نویسنده: سیدنی شلدون؛ مترجم: کاوه رحیمیان؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، درسا، 1376، در 468 ص، شابک: 9646104118 موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان آمریکایی - سده 20 م<br />این کتاب دنباله ی کتابی از همین نویسنده با عنوان: «آنسوی نیمه شب» است. در کتاب: «آنسوی نیمه شب»، آنها بازی دلنشین عشق و مرگ را، به پایان رساندند. و اکنون، در «خاطرات نیمه شب»، نجات یافتگان، بار دیگر از یکدیگر دیدار میکنند، تا برای آخرین بار، به بازی مرگبار ادامه دهند… در زیر سایه ی فشارِ غم از ناشناخته ها، زنی زیبا، با ناامیدی تلاش میکند، تا از فراموشی بازگردد. این زن، «کاترین داگلاس» است که بار دیگر، دست سرنوشت، او را به مبارزه با «کنستانتین دیمیرس» خونخوار و بیرحم، برمیگزیند. «کنستانتین دیمیرس» یک یونانی از تبار کشتیرانهاست، که همسر «کاترین» را به قتل رسانده، و اکنون قصد جان وی را دارد. او که در اروپای رها شده از جنگ میچرخد، علائمی مرگبار به سوی کاترین میفرستد، چون تنها کسیکه از راز خیانتهای او آگاهی دارد، کاترین است. و ... ا. شربیانی</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1637873779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11979299595335833778">A story mixed with revenge, greed, romance and want for justice. <br/><br/>Catherine didn't have any idea how her life would become upside down when Demeris arrives in her life, not in a good way. He is trouble, ensuring at each point Catherine suffers. It is the sequel to The Other Side of Midnight but you will not miss out on anything much. The story is still enjoyable. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17043099553964397709">What a painful read this has been!<br/>Everything from the plot to the writing was utterly banal. This book didn't manage to quirk my interest at any point. The whole thing to me seemed blatantly stupid, to be honest.<br/>Characters, along with being hackneyed were also completely unrealistic.   <span id="freeText17043099553964397709" style="display:none">What a painful read this has been!<br />Everything from the plot to the writing was utterly banal. This book didn't manage to quirk my interest at any point. The whole thing to me seemed blatantly stupid, to be honest.<br />Characters, along with being hackneyed were also completely unrealistic. Especially, Constantin Dimires who was most ludicrous of all. <br />I've read 2 Sidney Sheldon books before this and one thing that I've found to be consistent in his novels is the dreadful writing. The language, as always, was extremely appalling and the plot even more asinine.<br />After this book, I seem to have developed a strong aversion to Sheldon's books, for good. </span>

<div id="review_357010023" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/357010023" />
    <a title="Jeremy Bates" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5709335-jeremy-bates"><img alt="Jeremy Bates" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600930582p2/5709335.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/357010023?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeremy Bates" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeremy Bates" href="/user/show/5709335-jeremy-bates">Jeremy Bates</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer357010023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6538368648549013916"><em>Memories of Midnight</em> (1990) is a sequel to <em>The Other Side of Midnight</em> (1973), what many people consider to be one of his best novels. <em>Memories</em>, however, holds its own mixing revenge, greed, justice, and romance.<br/><br/>I think it's a sign of a good book if, after some ten odd years, you can read it again and remember nearly all of the characters. That's what this one was like for me.<br/><br/>Demiris, the vengeful Greek billionaire; Chotas, the brilliant lawyer; and Catherine, the amnesic who just wants to fall i</span>
  <span id="freeText6538368648549013916" style="display:none"><em>Memories of Midnight</em> (1990) is a sequel to <em>The Other Side of Midnight</em> (1973), what many people consider to be one of his best novels. <em>Memories</em>, however, holds its own mixing revenge, greed, justice, and romance.<br /><br />I think it's a sign of a good book if, after some ten odd years, you can read it again and remember nearly all of the characters. That's what this one was like for me.<br /><br />Demiris, the vengeful Greek billionaire; Chotas, the brilliant lawyer; and Catherine, the amnesic who just wants to fall in love (the weakest character of the bunch, imo).<br /><br />Nevertheless, Sheldon is a master of plot. In fact I don't know anyone who writes as breezy as he does (a good thing), while throwing in as many twists and turns.<br /><br />I think part of James Patterson's success is due to his incredibly short chapters. Like them or not, it just makes you feel like you're flipping the pages faster (and you are because of all the white space!) Similarly, part of Sheldon's success I think is due not to short chapters but his short paragraphs. Anywhere he can fit in a break (#) he does. It's a good technique to keep things moving, and it allows him to jump all over the place and get inside everyone's head seemingly without effort.<br /><br />More than any of Sydney Sheldon’s novels, <em>Memories of Midnight</em> shows that the author comes from the movie and television script writing with its short scenes and generic descriptions of people and settings.<br /><br />The late Sydney Sheldon was the author of eighteen bestselling novels. He wrote more than 200 television scripts and twenty-five movie scripts and six Broadway scripts. He started writing novels at the age of fifty.<br /><br />Highly recommended.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6538368648549013916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1814918781" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1814918781" />
    <a title="Bren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61659069-bren"><img alt="Bren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590193281p2/61659069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1814918781?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bren" href="/user/show/61659069-bren">Bren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=trilogys-and-other-series">trilogys-and-other-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=dark-and-heavy">dark-and-heavy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=read-and-reviewed">read-and-reviewed</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1814918781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8141965497218675408">Sorry Sheldon. Sorry sorry sorry sorry.<br/><br/>It feels awful giving one of my favorite writer's books a two star rating. And this is not the only one of his books where I have done that but nine times out of ten I love his books. It is just that he has so many it is inevitable there will be one or two I will not like.<br/><br/>But this is the one that let me down the most.<br/><br/>Why? because it is part two of his masterpiece (one of his masterpieces) "The other side of midnight". That was not a book that, in my opinion</span>
  <span id="freeText8141965497218675408" style="display:none">Sorry Sheldon. Sorry sorry sorry sorry.<br /><br />It feels awful giving one of my favorite writer's books a two star rating. And this is not the only one of his books where I have done that but nine times out of ten I love his books. It is just that he has so many it is inevitable there will be one or two I will not like.<br /><br />But this is the one that let me down the most.<br /><br />Why? because it is part two of his masterpiece (one of his masterpieces) "The other side of midnight". That was not a book that, in my opinion ever needed a part two. But once I heard there WAS a part two I could not wait.<br /><br />But as with most sequels It was a let down.<br /><br />None of the characters in book two who were in book one seemed to be the same person. They really didn't.<br /><br />But most of all was the issues with Constantine Demires.<br /><br />SPOILERS FOR BOTH BOOKS IN THE SERIES:<br /><br />Constantine Demires was one of the most fascinating characters ever created. He was like Kaiser Soze meets Tony Soprano meets a nasty version of Batman. The master manipulator and a charismatic but mysterious and impossible to understand thunder bolt.<br /><br />Not in part two! Here he is literally a different person, the usual bumbling but dangerous villain. I could not believe it. In fact I was so upset that I prefer to pretend I did not read this at all. (sorry but..)<br /><br />Part of the allure..actually all of it..with Demires is his crackling intensity and utter brilliance but he is not dangerous unless you wrong him. Now in book two he is just a frantic killer and still obsessed with Noelle Page. Never! Not the Demires from book one. I was thinking:what on earth has HAPPENED to him?<br /><br />And Catherine? She just wakes up and doesn't tell anyone what happened to her? There was no reality to it. I also did not buy her love for the therapist. This was a woman who literally went crazy because of Larry. No way would she have been this..for lack of a better word..normal after all that happened.<br /><br />And the lawyers have done a good lawyer/bad lawyer role reversal. I felt bad. I felt like the book was phoned in. And I say that with so much love for the first book.<br /><br />If you are a fan of book one..or at least a mega fan..you maybe let down by this. I don't know. It is hard NOT to recommend a Sheldon book as I love his literature so fiercely. Decide for yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8141965497218675408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_954296171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/954296171" />
    <a title="Heena Rathore P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19253213-heena-rathore-p"><img alt="Heena Rathore P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597647146p2/19253213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/954296171?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heena Rathore P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heena Rathore P." href="/user/show/19253213-heena-rathore-p">Heena Rathore P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer954296171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5243940684311276786">Memories is a brilliant novel that keeps the juices of one’s mind flowing. It’s an ultimate page-turner. I love Sidney Sheldon’s books but this one is one of his best books. No matter how old the books are, or infact how many times you read them, they really keep you engaged!<br/><br/>This book is the sequel to The Other Side Of Midnight and rotates about Catherine (Larry Douglas’s wife). At the end of the first book she lost her memory and in this book, around a year later, she starts to regain it bit by</span>
  <span id="freeText5243940684311276786" style="display:none">Memories is a brilliant novel that keeps the juices of one’s mind flowing. It’s an ultimate page-turner. I love Sidney Sheldon’s books but this one is one of his best books. No matter how old the books are, or infact how many times you read them, they really keep you engaged!<br /><br />This book is the sequel to The Other Side Of Midnight and rotates about Catherine (Larry Douglas’s wife). At the end of the first book she lost her memory and in this book, around a year later, she starts to regain it bit by bit. This poses a threat to Constantin Demiris and he decided to take one last revenge with Larry Douglas (even though he’s dead), by sexually exploiting his wife and then killing her. He waits for the right moment for this but other loose ends, regarding Noel’s and Larry’s cold-blooded murder by Costa, starts to come up and he gets busy planning quite a few murders.<br /><br />Some new characters are also introduced and they play a major role in the downfall of Costa. This book familiarises the reader with the life of our beloved Constantin Demiris (past and present) and how he pays for all he does.<br /><br />Catherine meanwhile remains the main focus of the book and also the Costa’s target. After The death of Kirk Reynold’s (a co-worker whom she dates) in an skiing accident and two lawyer’s random deaths (involved in Larry’s trial) , she starts to feel that everyone around her die’s and goes in depression. Then she visits a psychiatrist named Alan, who actually plays a small part of our hero.<br /><br />The end is predictable but the way it is written is just amazing. You’ll definitely not be able to leave the book even for a second in the last 50 pages! Atleast I wasn’t able to. The end of Costa was quite unimaginable!<br /><br />I would definitely recommend it to everyone who hasn’t already read it, especially to those who love thriller and mystery.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5243940684311276786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

How might she know the destiny he has in store, or that her life is bound up with different casualties of his strong sense of self? From the extraordinary shores of the Mediterranean to post-war London, 'Recollections of Midnight' is an energetic, remarkable story of a blameless lady's battle against a frightening fate <br /><br />In this dangerous diversion, there must be one winner...If Judd is to survive he should play the amusement to win.<br /><br />“It will be a honeymoon, Demiris told her. <div id="review_950344055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/950344055" />
    <a title="Heena Rathore P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19253213-heena-rathore-p"><img alt="Heena Rathore P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597647146p2/19253213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/950344055?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heena Rathore P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heena Rathore P." href="/user/show/19253213-heena-rathore-p">Heena Rathore P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006178699" href="/book/show/869918.Memories_of_Midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19253213-heena-rathore-p?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer950344055&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer950344055" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2936283518092556808">Memories is a brilliant novel that keeps the juices of one’s mind flowing. It’s an ultimate page-turner. I love Sidney Sheldon’s books but this one is one of his best books. No matter how old the books are, or infact how many times you read them, they really keep you engaged!<br/>This book is the sequel to The Other Side Of Midnight and rotates about Catherine (Larry Douglas’s wife). At the end of the first book she lost her memory and in this book, around a year later, she starts to regain it bit by</span>
  <span id="freeText2936283518092556808" style="display:none">Memories is a brilliant novel that keeps the juices of one’s mind flowing. It’s an ultimate page-turner. I love Sidney Sheldon’s books but this one is one of his best books. No matter how old the books are, or infact how many times you read them, they really keep you engaged!<br />This book is the sequel to The Other Side Of Midnight and rotates about Catherine (Larry Douglas’s wife). At the end of the first book she lost her memory and in this book, around a year later, she starts to regain it bit by bit. This poses a threat to Constantin Demiris and he decided to take one last revenge with Larry Douglas (even though he’s dead), by sexually exploiting his wife and then killing her. He waits for the right moment for this but other loose ends, regarding Noel’s and Larry’s cold-blooded murder by Costa, starts to come up and he gets busy planning quite a few murders.<br />Some new characters are also introduced and they play a major role in the downfall of Costa. This book familiarises the reader with the life of our beloved Constantin Demiris (past and present) and how he pays for all he does.<br />Catherine meanwhile remains the main focus of the book and also the Costa’s target. After The death of Kirk Reynold’s (a co-worker whom she dates) in an skiing accident and two lawyer’s random deaths (involved in Larry’s trial) , she starts to feel that everyone around her die’s and goes in depression. Then she visits a psychiatrist named Alan, who actually plays a small part of our hero.<br />The end is predictable but the way it is written is just amazing. You’ll definitely not be able to leave the book even for a second in the last 50 pages! Atleast I wasn't able to. The end of Costa was quite unimaginable!<br />I would definitely recommend it to everyone who hasn't already read it, especially to those who love thriller and mystery.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2936283518092556808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_346444016" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/346444016" />
    <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas"><img alt="Benjamin Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451660582p2/4209082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/346444016?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Thomas" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer346444016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8862162927582443824">This is the sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/136167.The_Other_Side_of_Midnight' title='The Other Side of Midnight by Sidney Sheldon' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Other Side of Midnight</a> and a worthy sequel all round. While the first was published in 1973, it wasn't until 1990 that this sequel was published. And since the first could have easily stood alone, I feel sure the author bowed to reader and publisher demand to provide a follow-up. Often that scenario ends in disaster for the second book but that's not the case here.<br/><br/>This is basically a book of double-crossing. I mean everybody double and triple crosses everybody else in t</span>
  <span id="freeText8862162927582443824" style="display:none">This is the sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/136167.The_Other_Side_of_Midnight" title="The Other Side of Midnight by Sidney Sheldon" rel="nofollow noopener">The Other Side of Midnight</a> and a worthy sequel all round. While the first was published in 1973, it wasn't until 1990 that this sequel was published. And since the first could have easily stood alone, I feel sure the author bowed to reader and publisher demand to provide a follow-up. Often that scenario ends in disaster for the second book but that's not the case here.<br /><br />This is basically a book of double-crossing. I mean everybody double and triple crosses everybody else in this story and so the fun of reading it becomes trying to figure out just how it's going to be done. One of the main characters from the first book is back, Catherine Alexander, but unfortunately, she is the patsy for all the other characters and batted about like a ping pong ball throughout the plot. For those readers of the first book who were left unfulfilled because not all story lines were fully resolved or for those that needed to have justice for the "bad" guys, then this is a must read.<br /><br />Overall a fun book to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8862162927582443824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10043440235729298110" style="display:none">Tip for anybody wanting to read this book... YOU HAVE TO READ PART ONE FIRST!!! PART ONE IS OTHER SIDE OF MIDNIGHT. YOU NEED TO READ THAT BOOK TO UNDERSTAND THIS. both of them are GREAT!<br />people dont like this book because they have not read other side of midnight. both books are outstanding and are a must read for any mystery lover. I was thoroughly gripped by this book.<br />However... i will give this book a lower rating only because throughout the book Catherine is getting serious with guys she does not even know. but i wont tell you what happens to her.and also... i was not satisfied with the ending. the ending was not what i wanted.<br />other than that... it was extremely good and i highly recommend Other side of midnight and Memories of midnight.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13396405654349905031">So, if anyone figures out that Catherine is alive and not murdered Demiris' whole house of cards come tumbling down. As she regains her memory in that convent where he has immured her he starts to get nervous. So naturally, his strategy to prevent anyone from finding out Catherine isn't quite as dead as generally thought is to a) bring her to his home where everyone, from his estranged wife to the gardener would (or should) recognize her, b) give her a high-profile job (under a fake name--that'l</span>
  <span id="freeText13396405654349905031" style="display:none">So, if anyone figures out that Catherine is alive and not murdered Demiris' whole house of cards come tumbling down. As she regains her memory in that convent where he has immured her he starts to get nervous. So naturally, his strategy to prevent anyone from finding out Catherine isn't quite as dead as generally thought is to a) bring her to his home where everyone, from his estranged wife to the gardener would (or should) recognize her, b) give her a high-profile job (under a fake name--that'll do it! Not like anyone's seen her pic in the press from last year's Murder Trial of the Century) in his high-profile sprawling conglomerate corporation, c) hold his breath and hope she doesn't contact anyone from her past, as any normal person in her situation would do. Because if she does, he'll have to kill that "anyone". One guy who gets a little too close to uncovering the truth--from what Catherine personally tells him, which he fails to connect to said ballyhooed Trial of the Century; apparently HE'S been in a convent--IS murdered on the evil billionaire's orders; an old friend from the States is saved when Catherine decides against phoning him. Thank goodness she doesn't call an old college buddy who might spread the exciting news; Demiris would have had to wipe out the whole sorority. <br /><br />Sorry, but given this preposterous premise, it's really irrelevant to discuss whether the book is, in "literary" terms, good or bad (is it a spoiler to tell you it's rotten?) I swiped this thing from the reading room of the convalescent hospital where my elderly mother was a patient. It is the only book I've ever stolen that I returned. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1524483128" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1524483128" />
    <a title="Anish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30233357-anish"><img alt="Anish" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1524483128?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anish" href="/user/show/30233357-anish">Anish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1524483128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12758977475808127958">I had no idea that this book had a prequel until I finished it. This worked pretty much well as a standalone as well. This is my second Sheldon book after Doomsday Conspiracy so I naturally had my expectations high. The first few chapters were intriguing but Catherine Alexander was annoying as she did not have the least interest to know about her past but too desperate for sex. Constantin Demiris was great as the egoistic and arrogant billionaire who wore a charming face as a mask. Other charact</span>
  <span id="freeText12758977475808127958" style="display:none">I had no idea that this book had a prequel until I finished it. This worked pretty much well as a standalone as well. This is my second Sheldon book after Doomsday Conspiracy so I naturally had my expectations high. The first few chapters were intriguing but Catherine Alexander was annoying as she did not have the least interest to know about her past but too desperate for sex. Constantin Demiris was great as the egoistic and arrogant billionaire who wore a charming face as a mask. Other characters like Melina Demiris, Syprous Lambrou, Tony Rizzoli etc kept the book going really well. <br /><br />Some twists were decent enough and Sheldon used his knowledge about criminals and gave an excellent portrayal of them. But this doesn't guarantee a five star rating. Towards the end twists turned out to be predictable and sometimes mediocre. Climax was simply horrible. Some people seemed to have a liking for the 'Vintage' Sheldon but this is just the average thriller book you'll get to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12758977475808127958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16811283848519506365">Having read ''The Other Side of Midnight'' last year, I had no idea that it had a sequel. Surprisingly, the sequel ''Memories of Midnight'' is far more hypnotic and gripping with an engaging plot. An amazing book with a vivid tale capturing the influence and the influential and mastery over human emotions. I personally had goosebumps and strong adrenaline rush as the story neared the climax. <br/>About my favorite character in the book: Greek tycoon Constantin Demiris, a charismatic multimillionaire,</span>
  <span id="freeText16811283848519506365" style="display:none">Having read ''The Other Side of Midnight'' last year, I had no idea that it had a sequel. Surprisingly, the sequel ''Memories of Midnight'' is far more hypnotic and gripping with an engaging plot. An amazing book with a vivid tale capturing the influence and the influential and mastery over human emotions. I personally had goosebumps and strong adrenaline rush as the story neared the climax. <br />About my favorite character in the book: Greek tycoon Constantin Demiris, a charismatic multimillionaire, who doesn't know the meaning of defeat and likes his plate of revenge ice-cold. In the end, he gets trapped by his own wife Melina, and pays the consequences for his deeds., meeting a tragic end. <br />All in all, the book is an ideal best seller with its turnaround plots and twists and mystery. One phrase that would do justice in describing the book- '' un-put-downable'' :D</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2569784291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9732909887724881451">Memories of Midnight was as good as the first part, which is not very common among books.<br/><br/>I liked how we got to see all aspects of Constantin Demeris, and delve deeper into his life. Also, Napoleon Chotas. The new characters introduced too were very well done. And Catharine, I absolutely... Pity her? Hate her? I don't know. She was still a ping-pong ball being bounced about by everyone.<br/><br/>This story was more like a story of betrayals. Everyone was double-crossing every third person, which made the n</span>
  <span id="freeText9732909887724881451" style="display:none">Memories of Midnight was as good as the first part, which is not very common among books.<br /><br />I liked how we got to see all aspects of Constantin Demeris, and delve deeper into his life. Also, Napoleon Chotas. The new characters introduced too were very well done. And Catharine, I absolutely... Pity her? Hate her? I don't know. She was still a ping-pong ball being bounced about by everyone.<br /><br />This story was more like a story of betrayals. Everyone was double-crossing every third person, which made the novel more compelling. And the twists are pretty good. <br /><br />And also, Sheldon has done a pretty decent job of familiarizing the reader with the story of the previous book and the characters. Well, it felt a bit repetitive, but as a result this book may, as well, be read as a stand-alone.<br /><br />I would definitely be getting my hands on more of Sheldon's works as soon as possible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9732909887724881451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8F3PfBHWgQeSTLPzv5vsIt/dzbGsbVOCHKL5OmdvTPL+emICtbdCaWvHdPJykU4yQLcHpXWzbD1451Jc0Oky8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('P1I8noDva3S7sWlwsg90wIdq8HpIXjigbqxdZKni1VkxdZHgJI6oGkI6rnF/BdbQGAA6bpGABx8K6fYCHmSrWw==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer2445209646806832910">Sidney Sheldon (1917-2007) was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist.<br/><br/>His TV works spanned a twenty-year period during which he created <i>I Dream of Jeannie</i> (1965-70), <i>Hart to Hart</i> (1979-84), and <i>The Patty Duke Show</i> (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling no</span>
  <span id="freeText2445209646806832910" style="display:none">Sidney Sheldon (1917-2007) was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist.<br /><br />His TV works spanned a twenty-year period during which he created <i>I Dream of Jeannie</i> (1965-70), <i>Hart to Hart</i> (1979-84), and <i>The Patty Duke Show</i> (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling novels such as <i>Master of the Game</i> (1982), <i>The Other Side of Midnight</i> (1973) and <i>Rage of Angels</i> (1980) that he became most famous.</span>
